## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the canonical form of population dynamics ODEs. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth mechanisms such as logistic, Allee effects, or generalized growth models.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak/multiplicative): dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (power-law density dependence at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic minus catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized sigmoidal growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest polynomial density dependence)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (bistability or Allee-type effects)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (periodic environmental variation)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate minus linear death)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional or superlinear growth scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt ∝ P) → exponential growth regime, density-independent
- Quadratic term P*(1-cP) or P - cP² → logistic-type density-dependent regulation with carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P with sign changes → Allee effect or bistable population dynamics
- Logarithmic coupling P*log(c/P) → Gompertz-type growth, asymmetric sigmoid trajectory
- Difference of power laws (P^a - P^b) → Von Bertalanffy or metabolic scaling models
- Sinusoidal time dependence multiplied by growth term → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → saturating per-capita resource competition (contest competition)
- Product of multiple factors P*(P-c1)*(c2-P) → multi-equilibrium dynamics with unstable and stable fixed points
- Exponential time factor exp(c*t) modulating growth → non-stationary environment or evolutionary adaptation
- dP_dt = 0 at specific P values → equilibrium points; number and stability determine qualitative dynamics
